colname="col3" align="center">0.8</entry><entry colname="col4" align="center">In situ XRD, SAED, XANES, XPS</entry><entry colname="col5" align="center"><link href="#adma201700606-bib-0045"/></entry></row></tbody></tgroup></table><noteGroup><note xml:id="adma201700606-tbl2-note-0001"><label><sup>a)</sup></label><p>XANES: X‐ray absorption near edge structure</p></note><note xml:id="adma201700606-tbl2-note-0002"><label><sup>b)</sup></label><p>XPS: X‐ray photoelectron spectroscopy</p></note><note xml:id="adma201700606-tbl2-note-0003"><label><sup>c)</sup></label><p>SAED: selected‐area electron diffraction.</p></note></noteGroup></tabular><p>Kim et al. obtained 400 mesh FeS<sub>2</sub> particles by ball milling and further sieving.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0155"/> The initial discharge capacity was 447 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. As expected, the bare FeS<sub>2</sub> suffered a severe capacity loss, and only 70 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> remained after 50 cycles. The bad cycling performance could also be caused by the side reactions of polysulfides. Thus, ether‐based electrolyte together with a cut‐off voltage to control the discharge products has been used for the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Na battery system, and a long‐cycle‐life FeS<sub>2</sub>/Na battery has been achieved. Chen and co‐workers prepared FeS<sub>2</sub> microspheres through solvothermal reaction. 1 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub>/diglyme was selected as the optimized electrolyte, and a terminal voltage of 0.8 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) was applied (<b>Figure</b> <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0010"><b>10</b></link>a).<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0055"/> The optimized FeS<sub>2</sub>/Na batteries showed great stability at −50, 25, and 50 °C, and a typical capacity of 205 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved with no degradation after 20 000 cycles (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0010"/>b,c). Even at an ultrahigh current density of 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the battery still had a stable capacity of 170 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Although controlling the terminal voltage to 0.8 V was responsible for the low discharge capacity, the discharge product Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> led to better cycling performance, and made the battery a suitable candidate for commercialization. Meanwhile, both the intermediates and the discharge products were sodium iron sulfides, which were shown to be metallic‐type conductive by DFT calculations. By analyzing the CV data, pseudocapacitance was found to contribute a 46% fraction of the total charge transfer (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0010"/>d). These two advantages guaranteed superior rate performance. Very recently, Zhang et al. synthesized Co‐doped FeS<sub>2</sub> nanospheres, and by trying different Co ratios, the optimized Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>S<sub>2</sub> was confirmed to be the best choice.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0045"/> After Co doping, the discharge capacity at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> was improved to 261 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, which was achieved by applying the cut‐off discharge voltage at 0.8 V and 1 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub>/diglyme as electrolyte.</p><figure xml:id="adma201700606-fig-0010"><mediaResourceGroup><mediaResource href="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-fig-0010" alt="image"/><mediaResource mimeType="image/png" href="graphic/adma201700606-fig-0010-m.png" rendition="webHiRes" alt="image"/></mediaResourceGroup><caption>Performance of FeS<sub>2</sub> microspheres. The cycling performance with a) different voltage ranges, b) different kinds of electrolytes, and c) 1 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub> in diglyme as electrolyte. d) Pseudocapacitance contribution measured from the CV data. Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0055"/> Copyright 2015, Royal Society of Chemistry.</caption></figure><p>Iron disulfide as one of the most promising candidates for next‐generation rechargeable sodium batteries has several strong advantages. Although, FeS<sub>2</sub> suffers from great capacity loss in the full charge/discharge voltage range, a reasonable electrolyte choice and cut‐off voltage can lead to excellent cycling and rate properties. Yu and co‐workers have published a sulfuration method to prepare FeS<sub>2</sub>/C composites as anode materials for LIBs.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0156"/> No such report focusing on the carbon modification of FeS<sub>2</sub> for SIBs has been reported, however.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0240"><label role="interim">4.1.2</label><title type="main">FeS</title><p>Compared with FeS<sub>2</sub>, iron sulfide (FeS) features a lower theoretical capacity of 609 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. FeS belongs to the hexagonal cell system with the space group <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i>. During the discharging process, FeS first turns into Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> with Fe after sodiation (Equation <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0008"/>). Then, in the fully discharged state (about 0.1 V), iron and Na<sub>2</sub>S are found (Equation <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0009"/>). Some reports claimed that Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> was the final charge product in the subsequent charging process, which indicated that the whole electrochemical reaction was not reversible.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0043"/> The <i>x</i> value was 0.23, and the valence of Fe in Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> was (2 − <i>x</i>). Lee et al., however, reported that the FeS could be reproduced in the fully charged state<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0157"/><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0008"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0010.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0010"/></displayedItem><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0009"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0011.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0011"/></displayedItem></p><p>FeS obtained through a mechanical alloying method was reported as anode material for SIBs by Kim et al.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0155"/> The initial discharge capacity was 610 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, but it dropped quickly during the next 150 cycles, and only 195 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> remained. The possible reason for the bad cycling performance is likely to be the large volume changes and the presence of sodium polysulfides. Later research focused on carbon modification to improve the electrochemical performance. Wu et al. used the solvothermal method and L‐proline as their carbon and nitrogen source to obtain N‐doped FeS/C microspheres (FeS/CN).<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0158"/> Owing to the SEI film, FeS/CN displayed a very low Coulombic efficiency of about 52.6% and high irreversible capacity (706 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>) in the first cycle at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. The capacity was 354.5 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles. Lee et al. prepared FeS/rGO composites by using spray pyrolysis and a sulfuration treatment.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0157"/> After rGO modification, FeS achieved high rate capability of 340 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 6 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Meanwhile, no obvious capacity fading was found in 50 cycles at 500 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Wang et al. prepared yolk–shell FeS/carbon nanospheres by using a spatially confined sulfuration strategy, as shown in <b>Figure</b> <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0011"><b>11</b></link>a.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0043"/> The galvanostatic curves at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and the CV curves are also provided in Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0011"/>b,c. The CV profiles show great shifts in the oxidation and reduction peaks in the initial two cycles, which was caused by the irreversible electrochemical reactions. The discharge capacities were 621, 584, 537, 505, and 452 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 100, 250, 500, 1000, and 5000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0011"/>d). The cycling stability test showed that the capacity retention after 300 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup> was 67.6%. From the scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and TEM images collected after 50 cycles, the nanosphere structure was maintained. This was because the unique yolk–shell structure provided large enough room for the volume changes during cycling. Nevertheless, the conversion reaction pulverized the electrode materials, and the amorphous intermediates occupied the void space, which caused capacity fading during long‐term cycling. Yu and co‐workers also fabricated FeS/C on carbon cloth as a flexible electrode by hydrothermal reaction.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0159"/> Then, the thus‐obtained colloid product was bonded with carbon cloth and treated at 500 °C in Ar. The easily obtained flexible electrode displayed a discharge capacity of ≈500 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the initial cycle and 430 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 50 cycles at 91 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and the discharge capacity was 280 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the high current density of 4568 mA g<sup>−1</sup>.</p><figure xml:id="adma201700606-fig-0011"><mediaResourceGroup><mediaResource href="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-fig-0011" alt="image"/><mediaResource mimeType="image/png" href="graphic/adma201700606-fig-0011-m.png" rendition="webHiRes" alt="image"/></mediaResourceGroup><caption>Yolk–shell‐structured FeS/C composites. a) Schematic illustration of the synthetic procedures with TEM images in inset. b) Galvanostatic curves at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. c) CV profiles. d) Cycling and rate performances compared to core–shell‐structured FeS/C and micro‐FeS. Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0043"/> Copyright 2015, Nature Publishing Group.</caption></figure><p>Above all, the cycling performances were improved by using carbon modification. Due to the possible sodium polysulfides intermediates and the large volume changes, however, the electrode still, to some extent, suffered capacity loss. rGO displayed much more excellent cycling and rate performances because of the large specific surface area and the high electronic conductivity. The yolk–shell structure also confines the active material loss and accommodates the volume changes.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0250"><label role="interim">4.1.3</label><title type="main">FeSe<sub>2</sub></title><p>Iron diselenide is another compound among the iron‐based chalcogenides. The synthesis methods include solvothermal reaction or combinations of spray pyrolysis and sulfuration methods. FeSe<sub>2</sub> features the orthorhombic <i>Pnnm</i> space group and a theoretical specific capacity of 500 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. During the discharging process, FeSe<sub>2</sub> is first reduced to Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeSe<sub>2</sub>, and then FeSe appears (Equations <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0010"/> and <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0011"/>). Finally, iron atoms and Na<sub>2</sub>Se are detected in the fully discharged state (Equation <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0012"/>). Then, in the charging process, quite differently from the iron sulfides, the reaction is reversible, and the final charge product is FeSe<sub>2</sub><link href="#adma201700606-bib-0160"/><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0010"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0012.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0012"/></displayedItem><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0011"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0013.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0013"/></displayedItem><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0012"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0014.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0014"/></displayedItem></p><p>FeSe<sub>2</sub> was first reported by Zhang et al., which was synthesized using ammonium iron sulfate and selenium in a solvothermal reaction.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0160"/> The size of the pure FeSe<sub>2</sub> microspheres was 2–5 µm, and they each were assembled from several nano‐octahedra (<b>Figure</b> <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"><b>12</b></link>a). Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"/>b displays galvanostatic curves of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/Na batteries with 1 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub>/diglyme as electrolyte. The changed voltage plateau indicates phase or morphology changes. The relatively high platform around 1.5 V provides the advantage of high safety for SIBs anodes, which is the same as for the widely reported Li<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>5</sub>O<sub>12</sub> in LIBs. Compared to the carbon–ester‐based electrolyte, ether‐based electrolyte delivered a stable capacity of 403 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, as shown in Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"/>c. The capacity retention was 89.0% after 2000 cycles. High rate capability derived from the pseudocapacitance led to a discharge capacity of 226 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 25 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Other reports showed improved cycling performance by carbon modification. Park et al. synthesized an FeSe<sub>2</sub>/amorphous carbon composite by a spray‐drying and the selenization method.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0161"/> A stable discharge capacity of 383 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 500 mA g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved, and there was 69% capacity loss after 150 cycles. Zhang et al. prepared FeSe<sub>2</sub>/rGO composites, and the discharge capacity was 408 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after cycling for 100 cycles with a capacity retention of 90% (compared with the capacity of the 2nd cycle).<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0162"/></p><figure xml:id="adma201700606-fig-0012"><mediaResourceGroup><mediaResource href="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-fig-0012" alt="image"/><mediaResource mimeType="image/png" href="graphic/adma201700606-fig-0012-m.png" rendition="webHiRes" alt="image"/></mediaResourceGroup><caption>a) SEM image, b) galvanostatic curves at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and c) cycling performance and Coulombic efficiency of FeSe<sub>2</sub> microspheres. a–c) Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0160"/> Copyright 2016, Wiley‐VCH. d) TEM image, e) galvanostatic curves for selected cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and f) cycling performance and Coulombic efficiency of urchin‐like CoSe<sub>2</sub>. d–f) Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0062"/> Copyright 2016, Wiley‐VCH.</caption></figure><p>Although carbon modification can effectively improve cycling and rate performances in carbon–ester‐based electrolytes, it still cannot fulfill the demands for FeSe<sub>2</sub> with long cycling life. Coated carbon or rGO may separate from the active materials after hundreds of cycles. Moreover, the sodium selenide may have side effects with and dissolve in the electrolyte, which is the most likely reason for the capacity fading.</p></section></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0260"><label role="interim">4.2</label><title type="main">Cobalt‐Based MXs</title><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0270"><label role="interim">4.2.1</label><title type="main">CoS<sub>2</sub></title><p>Similar to FeS<sub>2</sub>, CoS<sub>2</sub> can also be assigned to cubic phase and belongs to the <i>Pa</i><inlineGraphic href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0015.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0015"/> space group. The theoretical capacity is 872 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. The use of CoS<sub>2</sub> for SIBs was first reported by Shadike et al.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0060"/> The terminal discharge voltage was set to 1.0 V with the corresponding reaction <displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0013"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0016.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0016"/></displayedItem></p><p>On the other hand, another two reports proposed the following reaction mechanism<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0163 #adma201700606-bib-0164"/><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0014"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0017.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0017"/></displayedItem><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0015"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0018.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0018"/></displayedItem></p><p>Further investigation of the reaction mechanism is needed to determine the effect of the terminal discharge voltage. Li et al. synthesized a flaky CoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO nanocomposites.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0164"/> The cycling performance showed a slightly increasing capacity from 280 to 310 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> in the first 20 cycles, and then the capacity at the 1000th cycle remained at 192 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Liu et al. prepared CoS<sub>2</sub> in the form of hollow structures assembled from nano‐octahedra (H‐CoS<sub>2</sub>) by the solvothermal method.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0163"/> The stable capacity of 700 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> without obvious capacity fading after 100 cycles by applying 1.0 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub> in diglyme as the electrolyte.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0280"><label role="interim">4.2.2</label><title type="main">Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, CoS, and Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub></title><p>Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> possesses a theoretical capacity of 702 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> nanosheet/graphene composites were reported by Du et al.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0165"/> The charge capacity was 423 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and the capacity of 329 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> remained after 50 cycles, corresponding to capacity retention of ≈71%. The good rate property resulted from the highly conductive graphene sheets. Thus, at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the charge capacity can reach 154 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>.</p><p>CoS belongs to the hexagonal crystal system and has the space group <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i>. The theoretical specific capacity is 589 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. A sandwich‐like CoS/rGO composite was first reported by Zhou et al.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0166"/> Compared to the rapid capacity loss of bare CoS from 602 to 68 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> within 40 cycles, the CoS/rGO showed capacities of 567 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the 1st cycle and 231 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the 100th cycle (with both materials tested under 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). Peng et al. fabricated a CoS/rGO composite through a solvothermal method.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0167"/> The discharge capacities were 636 and 359 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 and 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. According to the long‐term cycling test, the capacity retention at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> was 88% after 1000 cycles. The CoS homogeneously dispersed in rGO matrix provided a stable structure to accommodate the large volume changes.</p><p>Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is also the member of the cobalt sulfide family. The theoretical capacity of 544 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> is less than that of CoS. As expected, the bare Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> had bad cycling performance.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0168"/> Therefore, carbon coating has become the most efficient way to solve this problem. Ko et al. synthesized Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> by the spray pyrolysis method.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0168"/> The obtained Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C composites showed a high capacity of 505 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, although the capacity dropped to 404 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 50 cycles. Zhang et al. prepared Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles embedded in 3D carbon nanosheet networks.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0169"/> Quite different from the performance in LIBs, the capacity loss for SIBs was over 50% within 50 cycles. Another method to prepare porous Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> carbon materials was using zeolitic imidazolate frameworks (ZIF‐67) as a template to react with sulfur powder.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0170"/> The discharge capacities were 380 and 300 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> for the 2nd and 50th cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to capacity retention of 77%. When subjected to a high current density of 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the discharge capacity of 230 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> was still remained.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0290"><label role="interim">4.2.3</label><title type="main">CoSe<sub>2</sub></title><p>CoSe<sub>2</sub> is assigned to the orthorhombic marcasite phase with a theoretical capacity of 494 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. The reaction mechanism is similar to that of FeSe<sub>2</sub>.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0062"/> In the discharge process, Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoSe were found to be intermediates. In the fully discharged state, the products were Co and Na<sub>2</sub>Se, and then, during the charging process, all the reactions were reversible. Zhang et al. synthesized urchin‐like CoSe<sub>2</sub> through a solvothermal reaction.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0062"/> The size of the urchin‐like particles was about 1 µm, and they were assembled from nanorods with a length of 20–100 nm (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"/>d). The platform changes were quite similar to those of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, as shown in the Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"/>e. The discharge capacities tested with 1 <sc>m</sc> NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub> in diglyme were 434 and 354 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Long‐term cycling stability characterization showed that after the initial 30 cycles, the discharge capacity was around 410 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> and was maintained for 1800 cycles (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0012"/>f). Other studies which applied rGO or porous carbon as supports also obtained good improvement of the electrochemical performances.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0171 #adma201700606-bib-0172"/></p></section></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0300"><label role="interim">4.3</label><title type="main">Nickel‐Based MXs</title><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0310"><label role="interim">4.3.1</label><title type="main">NiS<sub>2</sub></title><p>NiS<sub>2</sub> is a cubic phase with space group <i>Pa</i><inlineGraphic href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0019.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0019"/>, the same as cubic FeS<sub>2</sub>. The mechanism consists of multiple‐step reactions. In the first step, Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>NiS<sub>2</sub> was generated. Then in the fully discharged state, Na<sub>2</sub>S and Ni were the final products. In the charging process, all the reactions were reversible.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0173"/> Wang et al. prepared NiS<sub>2</sub>/graphene nanosheets (NiS<sub>2</sub>/GNS).<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0173"/> The capacity of NiS<sub>2</sub>/GNS was much higher and more stable than for the pristine NiS<sub>2</sub>. Nevertheless, according to the theoretical capacity of 873 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, there is much room to improve the electrochemical performance of NiS<sub>2</sub> because the only stable capacity of ≈400 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> has been achieved.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0320"><label role="interim">4.3.2</label><title type="main">Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub></title><p>Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> belongs to the rhombohedral crystal system. Owing to the low content of sulfur in the molecular formula, it possesses a low theoretical capacity of 446 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. As for the synthesis methods, Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> grown in situ was made from polished nickel plate or nickel foam by treating it by the sulfuration method.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0174 #adma201700606-bib-0175 #adma201700606-bib-0176 #adma201700606-bib-0177"/> rGO–Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> was synthesized through solvothermal reaction or spray drying together with a sulfuration process.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0178"/> In terms of the electrochemical reactions, it was shown in the discharging process that the Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> reacted with sodium ions to form Ni metal and Na<sub>2</sub>S, and then in the charging process, all the reactions were reversible.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0086 #adma201700606-bib-0179"/> Bare Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> that was purchased from Aldrich Chem. Co. was used for SIBs by Ahn and co‐workers.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0180"/> The initial discharge capacity was 422 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and the capacity retention was 81% after 15 cycles. Further investigations on material optimization, such as by Fe doping and electrolyte selection, were reported by Ahn and co‐workers.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0181 #adma201700606-bib-0182 #adma201700606-bib-0183"/> Go et al. used a simple sulfuration treatment of nickel plate and obtained Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> petals.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0174"/> The stable discharge capacity was around 175 µA h cm<sup>−3</sup> at 20 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. Shang et al. used nickel foam and treated it by the hydrothermal method, but the as‐prepared materials still suffered from low capacity retention of less than 60% after 50 cycles.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0175"/> Song et al. also prepared nanostructured Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> on nickel foam, but the capacity slowly dropped after around the 60th cycle. Other reports were on rGO modification of Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> composites. The cycling stability and rate performances were improved. Park et al. synthesized Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub> hollow nanospheres/rGO composites.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0178"/> The results showed a stable capacity of about 450 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> for 150 cycles, and a high capacity of 377 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 3 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0330"><label role="interim">4.3.3</label><title type="main">NiSe<sub>2</sub></title><p>NiSe<sub>2</sub> has a cubic structure with a theoretical capacity of 495 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. The mechanism was found to be quite similar to that of FeSe<sub>2</sub>.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0184"/> In the discharge process, the three‐step mechanism included two intermediates: Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>NiSe<sub>2</sub> and NiSe. The final products were Ni and Na<sub>2</sub>Se. In the charge process, Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>NiSe<sub>2</sub> was first formed, and then the NiSe<sub>2</sub> was reversibly reproduced in the charge state. Yan and co‐workers synthesized NiSe<sub>2</sub> nanoplates for sodium storage.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0184"/> The cycling performance showed great stability at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> and a capacity of 311 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the 100th cycle.</p></section></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0340"><label role="interim">4.4</label><title type="main">Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></title><p>Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> have high theoretical capacities because of their electroactive Sb and Bi, which makes them very promising as anode materials for SIBs (Equations <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0016"/> and <link href="#adma201700606-disp-0017"/>),<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0185 #adma201700606-bib-0186 #adma201700606-bib-0187"/> although some reports express doubt on the existence of an alloy reaction between Bi and sodium.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0188 #adma201700606-bib-0189"/> As for the electrochemical performances, due to the large volume changes, it is very hard to obtain good cycling performance. Bulk Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> had a very high irreversible capacity in the 1st cycle and bad cycling performance. The initial capacity was about 980 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, and after 50 cycles only 200 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> remained.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0185"/> In the case of the bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, although there was a very high initial discharge capacity of 1250 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity dropped to only 100 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the 7th cycle<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0188"/><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0016"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0020.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0020"/></displayedItem><displayedItem type="mathematics" numbered="yes" xml:id="adma201700606-disp-0017"><mediaResource href="graphic/adma201700606-math-0021.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-math-0021"/></displayedItem></p><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0350"><label role="interim">4.4.1</label><title type="main">Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></title><p>Methods such as carbon modification and nanocrystallization were used to obtain Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> with improved electrochemical performance. Yu et al. synthesized rGO‐supported Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanocrystallites, and the results showed a stable capacity of 670 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> with high capacity retention of 95% after 50 cycles.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0185"/> Hou et al. prepared a rod‐like Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/C composite.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0190"/> The results showed superior cycling stability, and the electrode materials delivered a capacity of 699 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles with a capacity retention of 95.7%. Zhao et al. produced amorphous Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> embedded in graphite composite.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0191"/> Even when subjected to the high current density of 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, it could achieve a capacity of 661 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>. Zhu et al. synthesized flower‐like Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> through a polyol reflux process (<b>Figure</b> <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0013"><b>13</b></link>a). The obtained nanostructure delivered a high capacity of 555 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and the corresponding galvanostatic curves are shown in Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0013"/>b. Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles embedded in a phosphorus–carbon matrix and flower‐like Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> were also reported with improved performances.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0192"/></p><figure xml:id="adma201700606-fig-0013"><mediaResourceGroup><mediaResource href="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma201700606:adma201700606-fig-0013" alt="image"/><mediaResource mimeType="image/png" href="graphic/adma201700606-fig-0013-m.png" rendition="webHiRes" alt="image"/></mediaResourceGroup><caption>a) SEM image and b) galvanostatic curves at different rates of flower‐like Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. a,b) Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0187"/> Copyright 2014, Royal Society of Chemistry. c) TEM image, d) cycling performances at 50 and 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, with the inset showing the Coulombic efficiency, and e) galvanostatic curves at different rates of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorods. c–e) Reproduced with permission.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0193"/> Copyright 2016, Elsevier B.V.</caption></figure></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0360"><label role="interim">4.4.2</label><title type="main">Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></title><p>Sun et al. prepared Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorods, and they showed a high discharge capacity of 957 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, but suffered from low Coulombic efficiency of 68.7% (Figure <link href="#adma201700606-fig-0013"/>c−e).<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0193"/> The main reason for the low charge capacity was that the whole electrochemical reaction was not totally reversible. In the first discharging process, the sodium intercalated into the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> structure and formed Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, which then turned into Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>BiS<sub>2</sub>. These two steps were irreversible and led to the large irreversible capacity in the initial cycle.</p></section></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0370"><label role="interim">4.5</label><title type="main">Other MXs</title><p>Other transition‐metal sulfides such as MnS, Cu<sub>2</sub>S, CuS, ZnS, and binary metal sulfides have also been investigated, but have not received much attention.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0011 #adma201700606-bib-0194 #adma201700606-bib-0195 #adma201700606-bib-0196"/> The theoretical capacities of MnS, Cu<sub>2</sub>S, CuS, and ZnS are 616, 337, 561, and 550 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. MnS and ZnS feature the same one‐step reaction to form the transition metal and Na<sub>2</sub>S. MnS hollow microspheres on rGO were reported by Xu et al.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0195"/> The hollow structure and rGO supported the cycling stability, which led to a capacity of ≈300 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> for 120 cycles. GO‐supported ZnS was synthesized through a microwave reaction.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0196"/> The size of the obtained ZnS nanocrystallites was around 20 nm, and the nanoparticles were homogeneously dispersed on the graphene surface. The charge capacities of the 1st and 50th cycles were ≈600 and ≈480 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to a capacity retention of ≈80% at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. For both Cu<sub>2</sub>S and CuS, the reaction mechanism for SIBs was quite different from that for LIBs.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0011 #adma201700606-bib-0194 #adma201700606-bib-0197"/> According to a previous report on the CuS/Li battery, Cu<sub>2−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S (28.42 cm<sup>3</sup>) had high copper mobility and a similar structure to Li<sub>2</sub>S (28.01 cm<sup>3</sup>). The Li<sub>2</sub>S was generated from the beginning of the discharging process, which made it hard to select a terminal voltage to avoid Li<sub>2</sub>S to improve the cycling property. In SIBs, however, the terminal voltage can be set with a cut‐off voltage at 0.4 V to prevent the formation of sodium sulfides. Kim et al. investigated the properties of Cu<sub>2</sub>S by applying the cut‐off voltage at 0.4 V, and the capacities were 294 and 261 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 1st and 20th cycles at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0194"/> The discharge product was found to be Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>Cu<sub>2</sub>S without sodium sulfides. Klein et al. tested CuS/Na with a full discharge voltage down to 0.01 V, and the initial capacity was around 750 mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, but there was great capacity loss.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0011"/> Only about 80 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> was left at the 5th cycle. To sum up, avoiding the presence of Na<sub>2</sub>S can be a very effective way to improve the cycling performance.</p><p>Binary metal sulfides were also reported with the aim of solving the large volume change problem during cycling.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0198"/> Choi et al. synthesized Ni<sub>3</sub>Co<sub>6</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/rGO composites by spray pyrolysis and further sulfuration. The obtained Ni<sub>3</sub>Co<sub>6</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/rGO showed great cycling performance. The capacities were 506 and 498 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at the 30th and 100th cycles, respectively. The capacity of 361 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> was tested at a high current density of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Other researchers replaced part of the Se in metal selenides with S to improve the electrochemical performance. Shi et al. prepared Mo(Se<sub>0.85</sub>S<sub>0.15</sub>)<sub>2</sub>/C composites and obtained high capacities of 440, 398, and 360 mA h g<sup>−1</sup> at 50, 500, and 2000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0199"/> Some studies also investigated hierarchical or homogeneous mixtures of different MXs or MXs with metal oxides.<link href="#adma201700606-bib-0086 #adma201700606-bib-0128 #adma201700606-bib-0148 #adma201700606-bib-0198 #adma201700606-bib-0200 #adma201700606-bib-0201 #adma201700606-bib-0202"/> All of these papers showed greatly improved performances, which can enlighten future studies on materials design.</p></section></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0380"><label role="interim">5</label><title type="main">Conclusions and Outlook</title><p>In summary, we have reviewed the MXs as electrode materials for SIBs. Because of the multielectron reaction mechanisms, MXs always have high theoretical capacities, which makes them very promising and advantageous compared to other anode materials. Nevertheless, the high capacity corresponding to a large amount of Na<sup>+</sup>‐ion intercalation also brings large volume expansion, and the general conversion reaction will introduce soluble intermediates such as polysulfides. Especially in the case of carbon–ester electrolytes, the intermediates will have side reactions with the electrolyte. These issues may cause severe capacity loss and safety problems, such as a shuttle effect that is similar to that in Li–S batteries. Therefore carbon modification, nanocrystallization, electrolyte optimization, and cut‐off voltage methods have been widely applied to improve the electrochemical performances. Carbon modification of MXs has been considered as the most basic strategy. Carbon materials with different dimensions have been selected, such as 0D carbon nanoparticles, 1D carbon nanotubes, 2D graphene, and 3D carbon spheres. All of them can provide stable support for MXs and high electrical conductivity. Nanocomposites are always the most favourable choice for material design because of the large surface area and short ion‐diffusion pathways. The porous structure can also provide a large surface area and large void space to accommodate the volume changes. Other methods such as electrolyte optimization and cut‐off voltage control can be adopted together with the above‐mentioned morphology design. Reasonable voltage control to avoid the formation of the conversion products, sodium sulfide, or sodium selenide, can yield long‐term cycling, and the optimized electrolyte can also minimize the side reactions and the irreversible capacity.</p><p>Layered MXs have become very popular in the past few years. The unique layered structure connected with van der Waals forces provides enough room for reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation. As the van der Waals forces can be broken by special reagents such as <i>n</i>‐butyllithium, this is a good way to obtain expanded layers, leading to higher capacity and fast ionic conductivity. In the case of the cut‐off voltage method, the long‐term reversible sodium‐ion intercalation may cause the layers to become expanded and exfoliated. Finally few‐layered materials will bring more capacity, including some pseudocapacitance contribution.</p><p>Although the recent progress on MXs has achieved impressive improvement in their electrochemical performance, several tough challenges still exist for future work. Most MXs have very complex phase changes, with an impact on the electrochemical reactions. Some mechanisms are still unclear, and competing ideas exist. A phase change during the first few cycles will cause voltage platforms change, have a bad influence on the cycling performance, and hinder application in practical use. Investigations based on mechanism and kinetics research are very urgently needed. Meanwhile, most MXs have a relatively high charge voltage platform, which is also a big challenge for their use as anode materials for SIBs. Therefore, low‐voltage materials such as SnS<sub>2</sub> are more likely to be used in commercial SIBs. Many reports (about a quarter of the total number of research papers) have paid attention to MoS<sub>2</sub>, but only a little research has been conducted on other MXs. There is no doubt that MoS<sub>2</sub> features good physical and chemical properties, and has shown much more promising results. Other materials, such as FeS<sub>2</sub> and Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub>, are also worth investigating because of their high abundance and low price. These great challenges have inspired us to concentrate on this field. It is expected that future work will provide much more encouraging and comprehensive results on the mechanism and performance of MX materials. Moreover, reasonable material design and preparation methods are also needed for large‐scale production. Some MXs may not possess the properties required for commercial use, but they are promising materials in some special fields. It is believed that MXs will show their importance in next‐generation energy storage and conversion devices in the very near future.</p></section><section xml:id="adma201700606-sec-0390" numbered="no" type="acknowledgments"><title type="main">Acknowledgements</title><p>The work was supported by the Australian Research Council through a Linkage Project (LP120200432) and the Commonwealth of Australia through the Automotive Australia 2020 Cooperative Research Centre (Auto CRC).
